# Cert Prep Unity Certified Associate Game Developer Fundamentals

> Become Unity certified and show employers you have the Unity skills they are looking for. Improve your chances of landing that dream job doing what you love most—making games. This course helps you study for the Fundamentals portion of the Unity Certified Associate: Game Developer exam. Using these lessons, you can validate your knowledge of game design and programming against a benchmark of profi

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals) | Intermediate | 12K learners

>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/introducing-unity?u=76281980&t=46)** You can use Unity to create video games, architectural visualizations, even complete films and animations and it's also used for many other purposes where VR, AR, 3D is needed.
>

#### Render pipelines 
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=0)** - Whenever you create a new project inside Unity, you'll do so from the project creation screen that I've launched from Unity hub.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=9)** On this screen, you have a range of different templates that you can use to initially set up and configure your project.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=17)** Choosing a template is like setting the DNA.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=20)** It allows you to determine initial settings, what graphical render quality you're going to have, plus a lot of others.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=27)** Now for most projects, nearly all projects, you're going to be making a decision between fundamentally two different templates.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=35)** These are the Universal Render Pipeline or the High-definition Render Pipeline.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=41)** But which one should you choose?
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=43)** What is the right decision for your project?
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=47)** Well, it depends.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=48)** If your aim is to create a project, a game, for example or an architectural visualization that is going to run on the widest number of hardware and devices possible mobile for example, web browsers, consoles, PCs, if you want your project on a lot of different types of devices, then your best option is to choose the Universal Render Pipeline.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=72)** The word universal in that title represents the fact that by creating your project, using that template it can run on a wide range of hardware.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=81)** Now that comes at the expense of graphical quality.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=85)** You can still achieve great graphical results but the highest quality possible in terms of graphics is reserved for the High-definition Render Pipeline.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=95)** This template can give you the best graphical quality but it simply closes off certain types of hardware.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=103)** So you want to choose the High-definition Render Pipeline for consoles, PCs, high-end graphical games, and those are the cases where you will want to use that template.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=114)** Now to get started here, I'm going to go for the Universal Render Pipeline because it gives us access to the widest hardware possible, whatever your project is.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=124)** So I'm going to select Universal Render Pipeline from the template here and simply give this project the name of URP sample, and then choose create to generate a new project here inside the Unity.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=137)** Now, Unity goes ahead and thinks about that It in creates and adds all sorts of packages as needed.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=144)** I'm going to resume recording after this loading screens completed inside the Unity editor.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=149)** So here we are inside the Unity editor having just created a universal pipeline template here.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=155)** This is the URP default project.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=159)** If you chose instead, the High-definition Render Pipeline you will end up with a pretty similar scene here.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=165)** It's just that the High-definition Render Pipeline has access to higher fidelity graphical settings.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=172)** But I'm going to be working with the URP here.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=174)** In the next movie, we're going to take a look at the Unity user interface.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=178)** And I just want to emphasize that whether you've chosen the High-definition Render Pipeline or the Universal Render Pipeline the interface is basically the same.
>

>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=191)** So that really doesn't matter.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/render-pipelines?u=76281980&t=193)** The key difference between these two pipelines is that they have access to slightly different features in some areas.

> **[7:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=467)** The hierarchy, the scene, the inspector and the project panel.

> **[7:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=472)** There are lots more panels to view.
>
> **[7:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=474)** But these are the core panels you're going to be using all the time.
>
> **[7:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=479)** Shortly, we're going to see the distinction here between the scene panel and the game tab.
>
> **[8:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=484)** But for now, these are the core panels.
>
> **[8:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=487)** The last neat trick that you can perform with any one of these panels is you can hover your cursor over the relevant panel.
>
> **[8:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=494)** So in this case, I'm hovering the cursor over the scene panel.
>
> **[8:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=498)** And by hovering your cursor over it, and on the keyboard pressing Shift Space bar, you can maximize that panel to occupy the entirety of your view.
>
> **[8:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=508)** So if you want to zoom in and take a closer look at your world, and your objects, you can do that by hitting the key combination Shift Space on the keyboard.
>
> **[8:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=519)** But of course, once I've zoomed into it, how do I get back out of it.
>
> **[8:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=523)** And that's really easy.
>
> **[8:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=524)** You just hit Shift Space again, to restore that view.
>
> **[8:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=529)** It's a toggleable option.
>
> **[8:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=530)** And you can do that with any panel inside the unity interface.
>
> **[8:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=535)** For example, I can move my cursor to the hierarchy panel, Shift Space to maximize that, Shift Space to toggle that again.
>
> **[9:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=543)** Every single one of the separate panels in the interface can be maximized and restored by using that shortcut.
>
> **[9:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/working-with-the-interface?u=76281980&t=550)** So that is a rundown here of the unity user interface, the core features you'll be using nearly all the time.

>

>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=148)** By switching to the game tab you'll get that view from the camera.

>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=164)** I can use my mouse in the case of the first person project to move my view around and I can use the W, A, S and D keys on the keyboard to move the character around using first person controls.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=178)** I can also click my mouse to shoot the weapon and destroy enemy characters.

>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=189)** Now, for some games like this first person shooter game for example, you may wonder, well, how do I stop it playing?

> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=215)** That will give you control back of your mouse cursor and you can press the play button again, to stop playback and restore the unity editor back to its normal state.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=226)** You can also enter and stop play mode by using the keyboard shortcut Control + P on a Windows PC or Command + P on a Mac.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=237)** Command + P begins playback of the game and Command + P again stops playback of the game.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=244)** These then are the fundamental distinctions between scene mode, which is designed to be for creating objects and creating your world and the game tab for testing the world that you have created.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=257)** As you build your visualizations annual games, you'll find yourself switching between these two tabs to test out the work you've created frequently.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/scene-vs-game-mode?u=76281980&t=266)** Unity makes it so easy to do that.

> **[7:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=438)** You can use W, A, S, and D, the D keys on the keyboard WASD, to navigate your view.
>
> **[7:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=446)** By holding down W, you will move forwards in the view, by holding down S, you will move backwards, by holding down A, you will move left, and by holding down D, you will move right.
>
> **[7:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=460)** And when you combine these with mouse movement, you have the ability in a kind of first person view, to navigate throughout the entirety of the environment, regardless of whatever object happens to be centered, you can simply walk your view to a completely different location.
>
> **[7:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=478)** And now, using this combination of shortcuts and controls.
>
> **[8:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=482)** You have the power, to completely control your scene viewpoint.
>
> **[8:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=486)** Moving that camera anywhere to get a great view of your scene and to easily add objects.
>
> **[8:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=494)** Of course, we still have the question of, once I've added objects to the scene, like the player character, or this sign, although I can move my viewport around, how can I actually move and change the objects themselves?
>
> **[8:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/viewing-in-the-scene-tab?u=76281980&t=510)** We will see how to do that in the next video.

> **[10:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/object-inspector-and-components?u=76281980&t=645)** So we've seen in this video an example of how every single item inside this hierarchy panel is a game object.

> **[10:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/object-inspector-and-components?u=76281980&t=654)** Game objects are made up from components and we can change the component values by using the object inspector here.
>
> **[11:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/object-inspector-and-components?u=76281980&t=662)** And this allows us to customize absolutely any object we add to the scene.
>
> **[11:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/object-inspector-and-components?u=76281980&t=667)** So this component-based workflow is incredibly powerful for allowing us to customize objects to behave exactly how we need them to behave.

> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=282)** You just need to use Play Mode tint, the way to access this is by moving to the Unity menu, choosing preferences and from the preferences menu, access the colors option and there is an option here in this section under general where you will see Play Mode tint that allows you to pick different colors.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=304)** I'm going to click on that color swatch and choose a pretty bright green color, something kind of like that and accept that green color and close the preferences dialogue.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=316)** Now, whenever I press Play on the toolbar, take a look at what happens.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=324)** I press Play on the toolbar but as I do it, the entirety of the Unity interface here glows a bright green color.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=333)** And so a great way to know when you're in Play Mode is to have Play Mode tint activated.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=339)** When the interface is glowing in this bright green color, you can still see the options but this color is telling you don't make any changes you want to keep because they won't save.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=351)** And yet when the interface goes back to its regular color, on exiting Play Mode, I know that any changes I make will be safe so long as I save my scene at the end of the session.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=362)** That's great.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/play-mode-tint?u=76281980&t=363)** That's how Play Mode tint can really save you a lot of time and making that common mistake that results in lots of changes being lost.

> **[8:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/packages?u=76281980&t=506)** We have here an example of how we can use the Unity package manager to import an additional package like ProBuilder and radically expand the feature set we have available here in Unity.

> [!info]- Semantic Content

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** fbx (4), png (2)
> **Definitions:** is a  (3), is an  (2)
> **Code Keywords:** default, (1), let (1), import, (1)
> **UI Navigation:** drag and drop (3)
> **URLs:** [blender.org](https://blender.org) (1)

#### Post-processing with volumes
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/post-processing-with-volumes?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/post-processing-with-volumes?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this movie we're going to enhance the visual appeal of our environment by using a volume component, which is part of Unity's post-processing system.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/post-processing-with-volumes?u=76281980&t=11)** It allows us to enhance the renders taken by our scene camera on the first person controller.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/post-processing-with-volumes?u=76281980&t=18)** Let's see how that works.

>

>

> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/post-processing-with-volumes?u=76281980&t=59)** This object in itself doesn't really do very much apart from it exists to add effects to our world.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/post-processing-with-volumes?u=76281980&t=67)** The next thing I'm going to do with this volume is select the object, and from the inspector, under the profile field, I'm going to click the new button to generate a new profile.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/post-processing-with-volumes?u=76281980&t=78)** This actually creates a completely new asset.
>

>

>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/next-steps?u=76281980&t=17)** We've seen how to import assets from a range of different sources, including the Package Manager, the Asset Store, and also our own custom assets made for meshes and textures.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/next-steps?u=76281980&t=29)** We've seen how to compose those assets into a scene and how to add functionality like first-person controls.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/next-steps?u=76281980&t=37)** And we've seen the full workflow for building a project from start to end.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/cert-prep-unity-certified-associate-game-developer-fundamentals/next-steps?u=76281980&t=43)** We've seen how to create the project, import the assets, build the scenes, and then even distribute that project as a standalone executable that we can send off to other people who can play and experience that project without needing to install the Unity engine at all.
